        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1339398264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4363005861973821916"><u>Update 09/23/17:</u><br/><br/>While waiting for February (!) release of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35297489.The_Sins_of_Lord_Lockwood__Rules_for_the_Reckless___6_' title='The Sins of Lord Lockwood (Rules for the Reckless, #6) by Meredith Duran' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sins of Lord Lockwood</a>, I decided to re-read <i>The Duke of Shadows.</i> Sometimes, re-reads can be disappointing. Not so on this occasion. I actually loved the story more. When I first read it, I thought the first part deserved 10+ stars but the second part paled in comparison. This time around, the second part had a huge emotional impact on me. Intense, unique, gripping, spellbinding and I can go on and on… It's hard to believe it was the a</span>
  <span id="freeText4363005861973821916" style="display:none"><u>Update 09/23/17:</u><br /><br />While waiting for February (!) release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35297489.The_Sins_of_Lord_Lockwood__Rules_for_the_Reckless___6_" title="The Sins of Lord Lockwood (Rules for the Reckless, #6) by Meredith Duran" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sins of Lord Lockwood</a>, I decided to re-read <i>The Duke of Shadows.</i> Sometimes, re-reads can be disappointing. Not so on this occasion. I actually loved the story more. When I first read it, I thought the first part deserved 10+ stars but the second part paled in comparison. This time around, the second part had a huge emotional impact on me. Intense, unique, gripping, spellbinding and I can go on and on… It's hard to believe it was the author's debut. I think this is the best of all Duran's works. <p>____________________________</p><u>07/19/15</u><br />I love Meredith Duran's writing and this book, her debut novel, is a powerful, memorable and very original story.<br />I'm not going to describe the plot as it's been done by many reviewers already. Let me just say that the first half of the book set in India in 1857 during the Mutiny deserves more than 5 stars. It is a powerful intense multi-layered story that gripped me from the start and kept me on the edge of my sit long pass my bedtime. I am still stunned by it. The masterful characterization, the vivid portrayal of events (be warn: some of them are very disturbing), the beautiful romance are all top notch. The second half, set four years later in London, looses the emotional grip it had on me. The plot, the characters became less interesting and the story started to drag. Still for the debut, it was an amazing accomplishment. I 'm looking forward to read MD's new story coming this month.</span>

<div id="review_131477851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131477851" />
    <a title="valee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2320890-valee"><img alt="valee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443365004p2/2320890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131477851?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="valee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="valee" href="/user/show/2320890-valee">valee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2320890-valee?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131477851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6620617632241694831"><b>MASTER PIECE.</b><br/>Is there a better way to describe this book? I don't think so. I just can't believe I've never heard a thing about it before a week from now, it amazes me to realize such an amazing read might have been forever lost to me if I it wasn't for one of the most amazing friends I have here on Goodreads (Ally I will be FOREVER GRATEFUL to you). I will say this is a book beyond compare in this genre, which is a lot to say as I have read a lot of hist-romances. OMG, where to start? I can't r</span>
  <span id="freeText6620617632241694831" style="display:none"><b>MASTER PIECE.</b><br />Is there a better way to describe this book? I don't think so. I just can't believe I've never heard a thing about it before a week from now, it amazes me to realize such an amazing read might have been forever lost to me if I it wasn't for one of the most amazing friends I have here on Goodreads (Ally I will be FOREVER GRATEFUL to you). I will say this is a book beyond compare in this genre, which is a lot to say as I have read a lot of hist-romances. OMG, where to start? I can't remember the last time I was this absorbed about a book. I spent the whole freaking day shut up in my bedroom reading without stopping. Seriously, I only stopped to eat, that's how much obsessed I got with it. I was so consumed with the story I forgot I was reading a book and actually felt I was living it. This author is amazing, she just does magic with words. I suffered terribly with some parts while I laugh and cried at the same time with others. I got so immersed I lost all track of time.<b> I cried the strongest once it was over because I didn't want it to end.</b><br /><br /><b>THE DIFFERENCE BETWEEN THIS BOOK AND THE REST IN THE GENRE:</b><br />Probably that the plot was way better developed than in most of my past reads. I felt so enthralled by it, I just wanted to keep reading in order to discover even more information. I had forgotten what it felt to be taken into the past, to really feel you were living things that authentically happened. Only books can do this, but not many of them can actually make you feel you're truly experiencing these events from the past. Only for this reason I will add this book to my 50-favorite-books shelf. Sigh, I just can't believe how inspiring the book was, how it transported me to a time where things you just can't bare to even imagine where common.<br /><br /><b>AN ASTONISHING &amp; UNCONVENTIONAL PLOT</b>:<br />While most books in this genre concentrate on describing the upper classes and their daily dilemmas, this author always finds a way to surprise us. In this amazing book, we read about a woman who was supposed to reunite with her fiance who was momentarily staying at India while England was trying to rule it. While she discovers he is not what she thought he would be she also meets the man she was always meant to be with, something it's clear form their very first interaction. We get to see how this romance develops while the mutiny of the Indians takes place.<b> Be ready and have some tissues at hand because you will accompany our brave characters through this very same revolution and suffer and witness some very devastating tragedies.</b><br /><br />To sum up I just wanna emphasize that this book is definitely a must read and a literal work of art in the hist-romance genre. The author knew how to give us an abundance of background information but without being aggravating. This book will always remind as one of my favorites and I'll definitely be reading it again some years from now.<br /><br />Moreover, the romance will always be there too, and it such a powerful connection between this characters that you will just want to weep for how strong this link between them feels:<br /><blockquote>"Words are not the only way we communicate, you and I. They never were." </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6620617632241694831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_42881543" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42881543?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fani *loves angst*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fani *loves angst*" href="/user/show/1133802-fani-loves-angst">Fani *loves angst*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=keepers-romance">keepers-romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=heroine-i-wanna-shake-or-slap">heroine-i-wanna-shake-or-slap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=favorite-hero">favorite-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=6-stars">6-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=mystery-subplot">mystery-subplot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=romance-historical">romance-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=tear-my-heart-into-pieces">tear-my-heart-into-pieces</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42881543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2809042099068445688">AMAZING!!! I couldn't read another book for a day and even went back to re-read the best parts as soon as it was over.<br/><br/>Part One: Delhi, India as the Indians' revolution against the English begins. <br/>Emmaline and Julian have known each other for a few days but have taken a liking on each other. They are both outcasts: she has been tainted after been saved from drawning from a boat full of men while he has a half Indian mother. Unfortunately she is also betrothed to Julian's cousin and life-long enem</span>
  <span id="freeText2809042099068445688" style="display:none">AMAZING!!! I couldn't read another book for a day and even went back to re-read the best parts as soon as it was over.<br /><br />Part One: Delhi, India as the Indians' revolution against the English begins. <br />Emmaline and Julian have known each other for a few days but have taken a liking on each other. They are both outcasts: she has been tainted after been saved from drawning from a boat full of men while he has a half Indian mother. Unfortunately she is also betrothed to Julian's cousin and life-long enemy. When the Indians invade Delhi, he helps her get out of the city. The scenes that follow are gruesome and intense, filled with action, angst and eventually passion. However, these two people tragically get separated in the midst of the war.<br /><br />Part two: 4 years later, London.<br />After 4 years, Julian still hasn't got over Emma, believing her to be dead and blaming himself for it. Emma on the other hand, knows Julian is alive in England but stays away from him, blaming him for the trials she's been through after their separation. After the things she witnessed, she is permanently depressed and sad, without spark for life. But she has drawn some magnificent -if too violent- paintings from the scenes she witnessed in India, that attract the notice of a nobleman who wants to exhibit them in London. She agrees to travel there to present them, hoping she won't run into Julian. Unfortunately, at the very first night, Julian sees her and that scene, where they meet after years, is one I read over and over because it was simply, heart-breakingly stunning. Julian wants to continue where they left off where Emma tries to send him away. But soon it becomes obvious that someone is trying to destroy the paintings or kill Emma or perhaps both, and Julian is the only one who can help her. <br /><br />Simply one of the best books I've ever read. Very emotionally powerful, heart-wrenching and angsty. It is not for the weak at heart and I can even understand it may seem maudlin to those who prefer lighter stuff. I suspect though, that readers who loved Private Arrangements will find this memorable as well, since that heart-breaking intensity found in PA is here as well, even if their plots are completely different.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2809042099068445688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_192223044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192223044" />
    <a title="Crista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3194546-crista"><img alt="Crista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284946251p2/3194546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192223044?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crista" href="/user/show/3194546-crista">Crista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=tear-jerkers">tear-jerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=hot">hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=tortured-heroines">tortured-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=tortured-heroes">tortured-heroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192223044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18005284644854895625">Sometimes in life you read a book that is so great, you wish you would've been more discriminate with 5 star ratings. This is definitely a 5 star read, and it makes me wish I had more stars to give it the credit it's due. This one was remarkable.<br/><br/>Told in 2 parts, the first half of the book is set in Delhi, India. This begins the story of Emma Martin and Julian Sinclair.<br/><br/>Although Emma is engaged to Julian's cousin, it is with Julian that chemistry sparks. Emma's fiance is a true villain. Selfish, u</span>
  <span id="freeText18005284644854895625" style="display:none">Sometimes in life you read a book that is so great, you wish you would've been more discriminate with 5 star ratings. This is definitely a 5 star read, and it makes me wish I had more stars to give it the credit it's due. This one was remarkable.<br /><br />Told in 2 parts, the first half of the book is set in Delhi, India. This begins the story of Emma Martin and Julian Sinclair.<br /><br />Although Emma is engaged to Julian's cousin, it is with Julian that chemistry sparks. Emma's fiance is a true villain. Selfish, unfeeling, and only interested in Emma's money. It doesn't take long for Emma to tire of her finance's antics and break off the engagement. If only that were the end of the story.....<br /><br />A rebellion breaks out between the English and the Natives. Emma and Julian are forced to flee Delhi for their lives. The suspense in this book is tangible. You feel like you are right in the middle of the chaos and horror as the brutalities of war are shed to light. On their journey out of the country, Julian and Emma fall in love. If only that were the end of the story.........<br /><br />Part 2 is set in London, England. This is an epic tale that spans many years and even different continents. Emma and Julian are separated during the war. Julian believes Emma is dead and Emma believes Julian didn't care for her and broke a promise. Whereas part 1 contains action and suspense, it is part 2 that will break even the hardest of hearts. There are so many scenes that will stay with me. The scene where Julian and Emma are reunited, the love scene in the locked room, the scene where Julian wants to recount the events of the past with the globe, and especially the final scenes of the book.<br /><br />Basically, this is a superb story about a man and his astounding love for one woman. Julian's love for Emma knows no end. He pursues her relentlessly. No matter how many stop lights she gives him, he pursues her. His devotion, love, and commitment to her is simply stunning. One of the main themes I will take from this book is the power of true love.<br /><br />Duran's writing ability is superb. The poignancy, emotion, and rawness of this novel astounds me. Save this one for when you need something special.....something "other". It is awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18005284644854895625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1709111897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1709111897" />
    <a title="Joanna Loves Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28993380-joanna-loves-reading"><img alt="Joanna Loves Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509424316p2/28993380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1709111897?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna Loves Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna Loves Reading" href="/user/show/28993380-joanna-loves-reading">Joanna Loves Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=hr">hr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=i-own-nook">i-own-nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=hr-geographical">hr-geographical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=mofo-dukes">mofo-dukes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28993380-joanna-loves-reading?shelf=arty">arty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1709111897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6907641038621197475">When I read this about four or more years ago, before joining Goodreads, I enjoyed it, but it was a bit too angsty and heartbreaking for me. With this re-read, I decided to move it up a star. Knowing some of the difficult parts ahead of time helped me be prepared and see it for the growth needed in the characters as they battled personal and shared demons. Things I love about this book:<br/><br/>1. Emma - she was an independent thinker, who didn't care what others thought, BUT she was still raise by Briti</span>
  <span id="freeText6907641038621197475" style="display:none">When I read this about four or more years ago, before joining Goodreads, I enjoyed it, but it was a bit too angsty and heartbreaking for me. With this re-read, I decided to move it up a star. Knowing some of the difficult parts ahead of time helped me be prepared and see it for the growth needed in the characters as they battled personal and shared demons. Things I love about this book:<br /><br />1. Emma - she was an independent thinker, who didn't care what others thought, BUT she was still raise by British parents in a British society in a sheltered way. She had prejudices to overcome and harsh realities to face. It made her seem real and tangible. She was a resilient heroine, a survivor, but sometimes that surviving was not always a healthy existence. <br />1. Julian - He's just amazing. Fiercely protective. He know exactly how to bring Emma out of her shell. I loved his reactions to her, even in public settings. Like Emma, he felt real and tangible.<br />1. Emma &amp; Julian together -- perfect together. Because their journey isn't easy, it is all the more sweeter.<br />2. The setting. The true to time descriptions and details without sugar-coating. Loved that it wasn't all in England. <br />3. Getting to see Lord Lockwood and his wife (the reason I wanted to reread this).<br />1 again because this is key -- Duran's easy writing style that wasn't heavy but gave us so much insight into the characters and the setting. Flows so well.<br /><br />Area that I think needed work:<br />1. The Bad Man and His Motives and the subplot associated with it. The villain is a bit too bad, too far. The mystery is a really huge deal that is wrapped up way too easily. The romance overshadowed this part, and that is a good thing. That is why most of us read HR, but on the flip side, when you have such major mystery like this one was, it didn't feel properly balanced and should have been toned down to fit with the story better.<br /><br />In the end, I went with five stars because the romance is a helluva good one that it needs to be up there with the faves, and my only problem is that my next read has some big shoes to fill. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6907641038621197475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7175137552013782697" style="display:none">As often happens lately, I'm in minority here...<br><br>I found the book interesting because of the hystorical moment it was happening in, not for the romance... <br><br>The Sepoy Mutiny was a very bloody and the horrors inflicted on the innocent were terrible...<br><br>From both sides... <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521116929i/25217158._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>first from the Indians ...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521116929i/25217157._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and, as retribution, from the British...<br><br>I loved how the hero, Julian, understood this horrible fact. He, as a half (or quarter) blood, saw how the Indian people were suffering under the British heel and, even if he understood, he didn't condone what was done by them. <br><br>The heroine, Emma, continued to be blind to this, even when the circumstances proved her wrong. Only after being confronted with cruelties from both parties, she did get it. But her reaction was wrong and continued to be wrong even when in England. Her paintings showed more than her actions.<br><br>Both of them didn't want to speak and explain to each other why they acted as they did. Emma, obviously suffering from PTSD and Julian feeling guilty without reason.<br><br>I hate when that happens in romance.<br><br>I didn't get why they wouldn't speak with each other. Why Emma didn't want to explain what happened to her and where she found the incriminating letter. If only they spoke many things would have been avoided.<br><br>Also, why Marcus choose to pursue Emma for her money only after she got reconnedcted with Julian? Because he knew that the letters were his because hse put the Urdu phrases on her painting? OK, that could be an explanation, but it didn't ring true to me. He was a villain since the beginning and I dodn't know why Emma spoke to him in the first place!<br><br>The love story between Emma and Julian didn't rung true too. He fall for her because...she's young? Beautiful? She was another memsahib. Maybe a little bit less idiotic than the others, but she didn't have anything interesting IMHO...<br><br>Also, there's too much internal musing all around...<br><br>So, just for the parts regarding the revolt this deserves 3 stars. Not for the love story!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer84076423366044281">Th last half of this book had me up ALL hours of the night last night. Fortunately for me, Sunday is a day of rest. Anyway, I’ve been wanting to read it for some time, but got caught up an audio format kick for a while.. <br/>This story is beautifully written with relevant (and meticulously researched) details throughout. It was surprising to learn it was the author’s first. Anyone who’s done a little preliminary discovery knows this book has won awards, and after finally reading it I can understand </span>
  <span id="freeText84076423366044281" style="display:none">Th last half of this book had me up ALL hours of the night last night. Fortunately for me, Sunday is a day of rest. Anyway, I’ve been wanting to read it for some time, but got caught up an audio format kick for a while.. <br />This story is beautifully written with relevant (and meticulously researched) details throughout. It was surprising to learn it was the author’s first. Anyone who’s done a little preliminary discovery knows this book has won awards, and after finally reading it I can understand why. <br />Once they meet for the first time, I was quickly invested in this couple. They’re soon thrown together in a situation where they become extremely close; relying on each other in a life or death situation. Unfortunately, everything doesn’t work out as planned (does it ever?!). They eventually find themselves in another situation where they’re given the opportunity to re-examine that trust and feelings they once had for each other.<br />I’ll spare a potential reader a book report. However, this story is in my top 5 romance favorites ever, and will be rereading time and again. <br />This story would especially be entertaining in audio format with a great narrator like Alex Wyndham, Darcy Stark, Mary Jane Wells.. you get the point - I’d be on board. </span>

<div id="review_134845005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134845005" />
    <a title="KatLynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435483-katlynne"><img alt="KatLynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296698899p2/2435483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134845005?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KatLynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KatLynne" href="/user/show/2435483-katlynne">KatLynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=g-historical-romance">g-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=smokin-hot-steamy">smokin-hot-steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435483-katlynne?shelf=favorite-treasures">favorite-treasures</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134845005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17000671198252883729"><b>5+ Stars</b> <br/> <br/><i>“I am half sick of Shadows…said the Lady of Shalott”…Tennyson</i><br/><br/>Another amazing story that held me prisoner until the last page!<br/><br/>This is my second book by this author. Ms. Duran’s writing is like a form of poetry; it's lyrical and smooth, full of dialog and emotion. And this is an emotional story; no fluff here. <br/><br/>The story begins in Delhi at the beginning of the Indian Rebellion of 1857. Ms. Duran has done an amazing job reminding us of the horrors, the prejudice, and the tragedy of this up</span>
  <span id="freeText17000671198252883729" style="display:none"><b>5+ Stars</b> <br /> <br /><i>“I am half sick of Shadows…said the Lady of Shalott”…Tennyson</i><br /><br />Another amazing story that held me prisoner until the last page!<br /><br />This is my second book by this author. Ms. Duran’s writing is like a form of poetry; it's lyrical and smooth, full of dialog and emotion. And this is an emotional story; no fluff here. <br /><br />The story begins in Delhi at the beginning of the Indian Rebellion of 1857. Ms. Duran has done an amazing job reminding us of the horrors, the prejudice, and the tragedy of this uprising involving the British East India Company. But do not think this is more a history lesson than a romance. First and foremost, this is a beautiful, tender, sensual, poignant love story.<br /><br />Emmaline Martin has survived a horrible tragedy. A tragedy so intense, she now suffers nightmares. From the beginning, I admired her courage. She is young and her zest and resilience is seen early on as well as her intelligence. One of the things I liked the most about Emma was her disregard for what London society thought of her. My admiration only grew when she defiantly opposes the betrayal of her fiancé. <br /><br />Julian Sinclair, future Duke of Auburn, is a beautiful man. Julian’s father was English, his mother Indian and he has suffered being an outcast from both societies. Both characters have endured suffering and now both will witness and survive much more. <br /><br />It is a beautifully written, unforgettable tale that includes conflict, drama and hot, sensual love scenes. There is anger and grief, humor, regrets, forgiveness, tenderness and compassion. It also has a heroine that I loved and a sexy, hot hero who captured my heart early on. <br /><br /> I laughed, I cried, and I rejoiced when the shadows were lifted! My only complaint is that I wanted more! <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One of my favorite quotes after they make love for the first time---<br /> “I’m here,” he said into her ear, as the tears came faster. “Emma, I’m here with you now. Listen to me, I will always be here.” <br />“Always, she thought. He said “always,” but he had forgotten to say finally. Finally you are here. Thank God, finally at last. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1009240228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009240228" />
    <a title="Addie H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16858463-addie-h"><img alt="Addie H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511793475p2/16858463.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009240228?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addie H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addie H" href="/user/show/16858463-addie-h">Addie H</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009240228" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12998193217265349738"><i>(Tropes: Forbidden Love, Opposites Attract, Unrequited Love)</i><br/><br/>I thought the 1st half was way better than the 2nd - the latter is challenging as they are both in very dark places - but on a whole another fascinating read.<br/><br/><i>- “You do not frighten me. You alarm me.”<br/><br/>- “You’re not meant to be grateful, Emma; you’re meant to be flattered. And perhaps a small bit flustered, if you can manage it. That would give me the advantage I seem to need one where you’re concerned.” <br/>She eyed him warily. “You’re being </i></span>
  <span id="freeText12998193217265349738" style="display:none"><i>(Tropes: Forbidden Love, Opposites Attract, Unrequited Love)</i><br /><br />I thought the 1st half was way better than the 2nd - the latter is challenging as they are both in very dark places - but on a whole another fascinating read.<br /><br /><i>- “You do not frighten me. You alarm me.”<br /><br />- “You’re not meant to be grateful, Emma; you’re meant to be flattered. And perhaps a small bit flustered, if you can manage it. That would give me the advantage I seem to need one where you’re concerned.” <br />She eyed him warily. “You’re being silly, I think.”<br /><br />- “You do not strike me as a Lothario. You’re far too serious for the part.” <br />“Oh? I did give it a small try, if you recall. And your mouth tasted quite sweet. But perhaps I was too subtle?”<br /><br />- He pressed his face fully into her throat. For the space of several breaths he remained like that, breathing deeply against her. Her hand moved up to grip the back of his head, threading through the softness of his hair. A strange impulse to grip him harder, to cradle him fully, had her biting her lip. The urge was animal. Unnerving. Entirely out of her experience.<br /><br />- He spoke against her neck. “Have I kissed you, then?” <br />“Not yet,” she whispered. <br />“Then you should be content.” <br />“I am certainly awake.”<br />He pulled away a little, just far enough to show her his appreciative smile. <br /><br />- “I’m here,” he said into her ear, as the tears came faster. “Emma, I’m here with you now. Listen to me: I will always be here.” <br />Always, she thought. He said “always,” but he had forgotten to say finally. Finally you are here. Thank God, finally at last.<br /><br />- There was so much to be said and asked between them. Being with her felt like charting the sea: there were marvels beneath, and they lured him, and he wondered whether he ever might reach the bottom.<br /><br />- “Do you remember?” he said, shaping the words against her skin, so the memory that broke over her was not visual, but physical. He had brought stars out in her stomach that time. She had liked it then but now it made her want to scream; it was soft torture, the drip of a water clock when one had a migraine; it exacerbated the pain she already felt.</i></span>

<div id="review_2101038019" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2101038019" />
    <a title="Sam (AMNReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67310619-sam-amnreader"><img alt="Sam (AMNReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540254857p2/67310619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2101038019?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam (AMNReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam (AMNReader)" href="/user/show/67310619-sam-amnreader">Sam (AMNReader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=scribd">scribd</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=book-hangover">book-hangover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=authors-to-try">authors-to-try</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67310619-sam-amnreader?shelf=best-heroine">best-heroine</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2101038019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15705583374283224349">Reread 10/28/18: I have no more words nor desire to try to sum this up. I’ll keep my 50+ quotes to myself for now. <br/><br/>*********************<br/><br/>There are a lot of thoughts swirling around in my head. First, I caught this book as a BR - I was having trouble bringing myself to read it otherwise for some reason so it was just the push I needed. <br/><br/>I'll probably recycle some thoughts from that forum as well as borrow upon others as a result. Also, spoilering for sake of that... <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/>So, when I went t</span></span>
  <span id="freeText15705583374283224349" style="display:none">Reread 10/28/18: I have no more words nor desire to try to sum this up. I’ll keep my 50+ quotes to myself for now. <br /><br />*********************<br /><br />There are a lot of thoughts swirling around in my head. First, I caught this book as a BR - I was having trouble bringing myself to read it otherwise for some reason so it was just the push I needed. <br /><br />I'll probably recycle some thoughts from that forum as well as borrow upon others as a result. Also, spoilering for sake of that... <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />So, when I went to bed after reading this late into the night last night, shadows and depth were two things that stuck with me from this book. Obviously that one is right there in the title, but as motifs, I thought they were masterful. Both characters are dealing with these 'shadows' and being so different and set apart. And both characters have unseen depths by others-and likely each other...and really the two go together so brilliantly and heartbreakingly in this book. Because this book did break my heart. <br /><br />Julian noticed Emma in a garden and she looks bored, unwell, and miserable. Neither of the characters seems to fit in their relative place, and Duran shows how the lack of fit when all appearances indicate you should fit can be a bit awkwardly painful and make one feel more alone. Julian is between world in a heartbreaking situation. And in each other, they find a match. Emma is, by her own declaration, fierce. Julian is sensitive and empathetic and sweet. The book is filled with lovely dialogue that would feel out of place in other books, but fits so well here. Duran delicately demonstrates the heartbreak each character has had to endure that led them to this place, to their vulnerabilities and ultimately connection with one another.<br /><br />I'm at risk of rambling on, and I just might eventually. I still have a lot of processing to do. Because if the first half of the book was in tone delicate and brutal, yet hopeful somehow, the second half was gut-wrenching. <br /><br />Normally if a character felt or did what Emma did in the second half of this book, I'd be so annoyed. In this case, you understand. You understand her brutal loneliness, her heartbreak, and the ultimate conclusion that she'll never be over it. Meanwhile, Julian thinks her dead with good reason and I really was cringing before their first reunion. As I was reading it, I was thinking "there are so many ways this could go that I won't like. I will be angry at one or the other of them" and guess what? I wasn't. His approach to her was flawless. His utter disregard for others; her reaction was equally realistic. After all, by their own admission, (don't get me started on the globe: ("You want my whole itinerary? I won't give it! I have given you enough!") he looked for her everywhere but in London. And that doesn't make things easier. At this point, of course Julian is completely devoted even if 'she won't have him.' He tries different tactics, confuses her, we get some great insight into Lockwood. In the process, we can feel his pain too. She seems cold, resigned to her loneliness.<br /><br />Emma struggles to both deny and accept him. She's still so heartbroken and afraid since she's faced so many terrors, and was so incredibly let down by him. And her fear is completely understandable. So here, instead of veering into "God, get over it already" it stayed very much in the "Yep, I get it" territory. <br /><br />Anyway, as I still process, I feel I'm only doing a plot recap &amp; reaction of what I felt was an incredibly effective, heartbreaking, beautiful romance. It felt so very unlikely yet so very real. I haven't mentioned how masterfully Meredith Duran says things like <br />"I am not blind. Words are not the only way we communicate. They never were."<br />And things like "You are not the only one who took that journey."<br /><br />Or "Water under the bridge" "Then a very stagnant river"<br /><br />I am just so impressed at how I could feel their heartbreak and their tenderness. Simply beautiful, elegant, and brutal. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="15705583374283224349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1679761464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679761464" />
    <a title="Desi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7480228-desi"><img alt="Desi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587479761p2/7480228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679761464?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Desi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Desi" href="/user/show/7480228-desi">Desi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679761464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18307472376403670693">The sheer effort it would have required to write this and the attention to detail in portraying a foreign country would have earned this five stars. <br/><br/>Add to that the dramatic portrayal of torn loyalties, the impossibility of belonging anywhere completely as a person of mixed race, the drama of warfare where no one wins and actually making the reader (who can never see the paintings) believe in the amazing artistic talent of a main character this was a testament to skill. <br/><br/>I liked all the main char</span>
  <span id="freeText18307472376403670693" style="display:none">The sheer effort it would have required to write this and the attention to detail in portraying a foreign country would have earned this five stars. <br /><br />Add to that the dramatic portrayal of torn loyalties, the impossibility of belonging anywhere completely as a person of mixed race, the drama of warfare where no one wins and actually making the reader (who can never see the paintings) believe in the amazing artistic talent of a main character this was a testament to skill. <br /><br />I liked all the main characters and even the pseudo villain was well fleshed out and not overly melodramatic. A few things here and there to question. Like why on earth the extensive holdup in reconnecting after the war upon their return to London. But nothing worth quibbling over. <br /><br />Duran's use of language is as usual beautiful. One is always bound to find a lovely turn of phrase or two in her work. <br /><br />Lines I Liked<br /><br /><i>“Her hair was an unremarkable color, a curling, sun-faded dun that, in conjunction with her pale skin, made it seem as though all the energy of her being were focused in the brilliance of her deep blue eyes”<br />------------<br /><br />“The man was unnervingly handsome—like something from a fever dream, brilliant and fierce, skin touched by gold and hair so black it absorbed the light.”<br />--------<br /><br />“I've been going about it all wrong. The first thing I should have said is that you are the most beautiful woman I've ever seen."<br />She laughed despite herself. "That's a clever sort of compliment, seeing as it reserves you the right to change your mind with the next woman you meet. As well you should, with me in such a state!"<br />He leaned forward a little. "Would you like me to remove the qualification? I'd be more than willing to oblige."<br />"No, that's all right. My looks aren't where my vanity lies.”<br />-----<br /><br />“She thought to sit, but her knees gave way. She made a controlled collapse into the dust.”<br />------<br /><br />“But what use was vision when appearances proved so misleading? He could not be defined by his looks, or his name, or by the moments she had shared with him. Even his current silence held a quality strange to her. She had never known someone who could seem so still.<br />But it served no end, did it? No matter how unnoticeable Julian made himself, he would still draw others' attention. Some people were like that; they could not escape criticism, because they never quite managed to convince themselves of the role everyone believed they should fill.<br />She searched her heart. It did not disgust her, this foreignness about him. How could it, when it had saved her life? But it unnerved her all the same. It made her feel, in an immediate way, just as this entire country did on a vast and impersonal level: hopelessly weary, terribly obvious, horribly helpless”<br />---------<br /><br />“The native populace simply doesn't have the resources, organizational or material, that they'd need to defeat the British."<br />The British. As though he weren't one of them. God, what a fool she was! He had all but said he wasn't one of them! And so had Marcus, she remembered.<br />She moistened her lips, struggled to find her voice. "You're Indian then. You don't consider yourself English. You are Indian."<br />His tone was dry enough to burn. "What nice, convenient labels. If one works for you, by all means, don't mind me. Few ever do, in that regard."<br />She peered blindly into the darkness where he was sitting. His words were so bitter that they curdled the air. Yet prevalent in her mind was not distress, but sadness. There were worse things than being alone, she saw now; there were terrible sorts of intimacy as well. "I have failed you. Or … disappointed you. You think I'm a narrow-minded fool, just like the rest of the memsahibs."<br />In the silence of the desert night, his inhalation was audible. "No," he whispered, and somehow, with his cat-eyed vision, found her hands. "Never that. Come out of there, sweetheart." Boneless with relief, she let him pull her forward, into the open air, into his lap. And in this wild darkness, in the middle of an empty earth, she grieved for both of them—indeed, for every human in this wretched world, who must face the trials life offered, negotiate the changes wrought by time”<br />-------------<br /><br />“She was riding pillion on Julian's horse; hers had drawn up lame, and was on lead behind them. Julian caught her hand where it sat at the front of his waist. "Fort," he corrected, rubbing a thumb over her palm. "Look again at the plateau."<br />All morning he had touched her like this, casually and constantly. She felt slightly drunk from it; laughter came up in her throat for no reason”<br />-------<br /><br />“Lord Chad was a master statesman, but his talent was for democracy. He had no defenses against a natural autocrat like his wife.”<br />--------<br /><br />“That was the best thing about Caro: she did not set precedents that she didn't wish to follow. Fidelity, jealousy, judgment—none of these appealed to her. If he disappeared for days on end, doubtless she would pout, but she would not castigate him when he returned. Her expectations were adjusted to the lowest common denominator; one simply couldn't disappoint her.”<br />-------<br /><br />“What is the Urdu, Emma? Where is it from?"<br />He had a gift, didn't he? Unerring aim. "It is no concern of yours."<br />"And so we are back to our fundamental disagreement, for I think it is. The Urdu is rather peculiar. I would like to know where you learned it."<br />"From a dead man." It was more than she had ever admitted. "And now, if you will once again permit me the pleasure, I will leave you."<br />"Again and again," he said. "If that is your desire."<br />"No, thank you," she said as she passed. "I am fond of finality.”<br />--------<br /><br />“Julian cast him a glance. They'd been friends since their salad days, drinking and pranking at Eton and later, at King's College in Cambridge. But since his return from the penal colony, Lockwood was a bit of an enigma. Mellowed, and frighteningly cheerful. Yet occasionally Julian got the unnerving sense that when Lockwood took his leave, grinning and joking and smiling, he left to go find something to smash.<br />"You're slightly deranged," Julian said. "Do you know it?"<br />"Yes, of course. Is that a sign of greater or lesser madness?”<br />------<br /><br />“After a minute—or ten, or twenty—she realized he was murmuring to her. And then, with a small shock, she realized it was not English he was speaking. It was a different language, that melodic, lilting tongue that her maid Usha had used, so long ago. Like yesterday. It made his chest vibrate. It was more soothing than English, like a lullaby, nonsensical, blank. English was so heavy. So desiccated and hardened by meaning, by pain and anger and even the jests and petty quibbles, everything under the sun that obscured the basic truth. But the sound of his voice as he spoke to her now, she heard the wind in it, the stillness of the night”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18307472376403670693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45378125-mou"><img alt="Mou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481556027p2/45378125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2022532724?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mou" href="/user/show/45378125-mou">Mou</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2022532724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2585319940881353544"><b>“You are not the only one who took that journey”</b><br/><br/>4.5 stars rounded up to 5 stars. <br/><br/>A fabulous Read!!! <br/><br/>I always liked Historical Romances, no matter how complex or simple the story is, I always liked its essence. But, This Historical Romance is something else. AND I loved it.<br/><br/>The first part of the book holds in Indian Subcontinent and the second part is on British land.   <span id="freeText2585319940881353544" style="display:none"><b>“You are not the only one who took that journey”</b><br /><br />4.5 stars rounded up to 5 stars. <br /><br />A fabulous Read!!! <br /><br />I always liked Historical Romances, no matter how complex or simple the story is, I always liked its essence. But, This Historical Romance is something else. AND I loved it.<br /><br />The first part of the book holds in Indian Subcontinent and the second part is on British land. The plot is based on the Sepoy mutiny of British Raj in 1857. <br /><br />I loved the story. I liked Emmaline but I loved Julian. <br /><br />Emmaline is extremely strong and courageous, what she endured in India it’s beyond explainable. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“They are all the same, British and Indian alike, those men who could commit such horrible acts of violence against the innocent.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Our hero, Julian is a Duke of mixed ethnicity, British (father) and Indian (mother). <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I take no offense at the mention of my heritage. It is my better, I think.” He smiled. “Or better quarter, though that lacks a certain ring. My concern is for the peace. While I firmly believe that England has no place in India-” Her huff of shock made him smile again. “Well, and I am part native, Miss Martin.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Julian has a strong personality. The whole book proves his love, loyalty, and responsibilities toward his people.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Emma, this land has been crushed by the English. Its wealth stripped, its honor trampled. You are not dealing with penny-dreadful villains here; you are dealing with embittered human beings who have been robbed of their dignity, their autonomy, their sense of self-worth. And that is what this mutiny is about. Not animal grease on bullet cartridges, or any of that nonsense. It is simply the inevitable result of everything the British have done to India.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b> “Those people are my people. Both sides” he said. “British and Indian, I owe something to both of them. It’s almost my… my duty to help end this bloodshed.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Julian and Emma’s Love is strong; it’s so strong that it survived through this terrible mess. I loved their Love and every part of it.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I'm here," he said into her ear, as the tears came faster. "Emma, I'm here with you now. Listen to me: I will always be here."Always, she thought. He said "always," but he had forgotten to say finally. Finally, you are here. Thank God, finally at last.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>“In love, my temperament found a new taste for life, it found a cure for the pain and a pain without cure.” --- Ghalib</b>
</i><br /><br />Meredith Duran, The author did a fabulous job. It was her debut Romance and I have to say she is excellent. The way she mixed British Raj history and the romance it’s truly commendable. She did her study tremendously. She explained Indian clothes, cultures, habit. She beautifully connected Indian gods of beauty, Lakshmi and Elephant headed God Ganesha with the story. She even used some line and words from Indian language (Hindi). All of the Indian terms Duran used are correct and the synchronization of these with the story is perfect. <br /><br />The book is full of tragedy so I wanted a happy epilogue very badly. I know I am sulking like a child, but I want an EPILOGUE. <br /><br /><i>
  <b> Well, there is one thing I didn't like about this book. There are enough scenes to describe Indian sepoys cruel rebellion, but there are no scenes of British Raj Injustice and cruelties. <br /></b>
</i><br /><br />So, 4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2585319940881353544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1482980697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1482980697" />
    <a title="Carol Cork *Young at Heart Oldie*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3752204-carol-cork-young-at-heart-oldie"><img alt="Carol Cork *Young at Heart Oldie*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562766597p2/3752204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1482980697?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Cork *Young at Heart Oldie*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Cork *Young at Heart Oldie*" href="/user/show/3752204-carol-cork-young-at-heart-oldie">Carol Cork *Young at Heart Oldie*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8364152-the-duke-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1482980697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5317517962309064459"><b>I’m not sure why it has taken me so long to read DUKE OF SHADOWS, Meredith Duran’s much-praised 2010 debut novel, because I was totally swept by this powerful and beautiful love story.</b><br/><br/>Accompanied by her parents, Emmeline (Emma) Martin is on her way to Delhi to marry her fiancé Marcus Lindley, an army colonel employed by the British East India Company. Tragedy strikes when the ship sinks in a storm, leaving Emma as the sole survivor. She is rescued by a passing freighter, but the knowledge that s</span>
  <span id="freeText5317517962309064459" style="display:none"><b>I’m not sure why it has taken me so long to read DUKE OF SHADOWS, Meredith Duran’s much-praised 2010 debut novel, because I was totally swept by this powerful and beautiful love story.</b><br /><br />Accompanied by her parents, Emmeline (Emma) Martin is on her way to Delhi to marry her fiancé Marcus Lindley, an army colonel employed by the British East India Company. Tragedy strikes when the ship sinks in a storm, leaving Emma as the sole survivor. She is rescued by a passing freighter, but the knowledge that she has spent time alone with a crew of rough and ready sailors leaves her reputation, among the Anglo-Indian, tainted by association. Emma discovers that her fiancé is no longer the charming man she knew back in England; he is now a philanderer, gambler and only interested in marrying her for her money. Emma is determined to break off the engagement.<br /><br />Julian Sinclair, Marquess of Holdensmoor and heir to the Duke of Auburn, has mixed blood – his father was British and his mother was of mixed British and Indian descent. He is torn between two worlds, neither of which he feels he truly belongs to and both cultures regard him with suspicion and disdain. Julian is aware that there is unrest among the Indian troops (sepoys) in the service of the British East India Company and fears a mutiny. However, the British authorities consider Julian an alarmist and fail to heed his warnings.<br /><br />From their initial meeting, it is obvious that Julian and Emma share a mutual attraction and I love how Ms. Duran develops their romance in the first part of the book. It is so beautifully done and I really believed in their falling in love.<br /><br /><i>She stirred, small twitches and movements. Soft, sleepy noises. He kissed her again, more deeply this time, and ran a hand down her side, to the swell of her hip. Her eyelashes fluttered up; color came into her cheeks. He smiled against her. Fairy tales were wasted on children. Until this moment, even he had not fathomed the power of waking someone with a kiss.</i><br /><br />I could feel how torn Julian is when he makes the difficult decision to leave Emma in Sapnagar. He wants to protect the woman he has come to love and also ensure that his Indian family are safe but, most importantly, he sees it as his duty to try to stop the bloodshed between the two sides. He is a honourable man and does what he believes to be right, unaware of how much it will cost him personally.<br /><br />Ms. Duran doesn’t shy away from portraying the horror and brutality following the uprising and some of the scenes are harrowing to read., but I feel this is crucial to understanding Emma’s emotional state and her motivations in the second half of the book.<br /><br />The second half, which takes place in London 4 years later, is such an emotional roller-coaster and I felt as though I was living every moment with Julian and Emma, such was the power and skill of Ms. Duran’s writing. Julian is full of guilt for having left Emma and there is so much anger on Emma’s side, believing that Julian had broken the promise he made and deserted her. I could understand Emma’s anger towards Julian, knowing all the horrific sights she saw and everything she had endured. It is heart-breaking to see how emotionally fragile she is and her paintings seem to represent a way of purging herself of those terrible memories.<br /><br />When Julian sees Emma for the first time in 4 years, his pain and yearning is a palpable thing but I love him for being so patient with Emma and refusing to let her go. Emma fears that should he learn the truth about her, he would surely reject her.<br /><br /><i>He was so sure his opinion would be unaffected by anything she told him. But he could not know what was in her head. What was in her. And he would not like it. He would recoil and she would not be able to bear it. Seeing him leave again.</i><br /><br />There is no doubt that they still love each other, but it seems that the past will always remain an insurmountable obstacle. Only when they are forced to work together to solve the mystery of who is trying to kill Emma are they able to talk openly and honestly and shed the darkness of the past to find the happiness they truly deserve.<br /><br />Marcus Lindley was truly despicable in his actions towards Emma and his betrayal and gets a suitable comeuppance in the end.<br /><br />I was especially intrigued in Julian’s friend and Emma’s patron, Lord Lockwood, whose story is told in Ms. Duran’s latest release <b>The Sins of Lord Lockwood</b>.<br /><br /><b>MY VERDICT: If you are in the mood for something dark and intense with an original plotline, fascinating characters, suspense and a heart-stopping romance, I can definitely recommend this book.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5317517962309064459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123557359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123557359" />
    <a title="Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn"><img alt="Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300839213p2/2310262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123557359?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quinn" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn">Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Quinn by: </span>
      Lady Jayne, Catherine
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=aar-top-100-2010">aar-top-100-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123557359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12402297507996582975">Firstly, I must thank Lady Jayne for recommending this wonderful book, and Catherine for endorsing Jayne’s rec. For some reason, this excellent read is not one that I have seen come up in discussion very much, or if it has, I have missed it. Given the buzz that surrounds other books, I’m surprised this worthy title has not generated more chat and am grateful that it was brought to my attention.<br/><br/><i>The Duke of Shadows</i> is not your average historical romance. It has elements that I adore in romance - h</span>
  <span id="freeText12402297507996582975" style="display:none">Firstly, I must thank Lady Jayne for recommending this wonderful book, and Catherine for endorsing Jayne’s rec. For some reason, this excellent read is not one that I have seen come up in discussion very much, or if it has, I have missed it. Given the buzz that surrounds other books, I’m surprised this worthy title has not generated more chat and am grateful that it was brought to my attention.<br /><br /><i>The Duke of Shadows</i> is not your average historical romance. It has elements that I adore in romance - heart-thumping action with the hero and heroine’s lives at stake, a couple that are perfect for each other and realize this early in the piece, a hero that is to die for and a worthy heroine, both of whom have seen more than their share of tragedy – all written in beautiful prose that is at times almost breathtaking.<br /><br />The book is set in two parts – the first being 1857 India during the time of the sepoy uprising. Ahhh, what can I say but that this part was perfection. India made for a wonderful setting, expertly and at times gruesomely brought alive by a talented author. <br /><br />The attraction between our couple during the initial period of peace is beautiful and, more importantly, believable. To then find themselves alone with each other and fighting for their lives makes their experience both more poignant and tragic. The author provides some exquisite moments of tenderness amidst the cruelest of brutality. Through it all, there can be no doubt that this couple were meant for each other.<br /><br />The second part, although set in 1861 London during peaceful times, I found more difficult to read. Having seen how utterly right the love between these two could be, I had a hard time with seeing them apart. I love me some angst in my romance, no question, but at times I felt some of the magic was lost. <br /><br />There were moments of brilliance in the writing, and I realise the trauma they suffered, but some of the actions and behaviour of the characters was still not convincing or understandable to me. I think we also would have benefited from seeing more from Julian’s POV. At times this left me feeling that this was just another good historical romance, instead of the outstanding read that it was initially.<br /><br />Of course, the author would then craft a scene that again left me in awe of her writing talent, and I was reminded again that this really was something special.<br /><br />I am wavering between 4.5 and 5 stars for this one. Either way, I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12402297507996582975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1203156315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203156315" />
    <a title="Silvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8214978-silvana"><img alt="Silvana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406031736p2/8214978.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203156315?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvana" href="/user/show/8214978-silvana">Silvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203156315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14527764176383701515">5 STARS and more!<br/><br/>So this what a book hangover feels like?! I have finished this book days ago and I still can’t let go of it. I had to google how to get rid of a book hangover but nothing worked, I mourned with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9536782-ash' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ashlee</a> who seems to be just as lost as me, tried other books to abandon after a few chapters.<br/><br/>One word for this book, GEM.<br/><br/>This novel is uplifting, heart-wrenching and heart-mending. The writing is faultless, the imagery incredible and the connection between our lovers scorching.<br/><br/>As I read, </span>
  <span id="freeText14527764176383701515" style="display:none">5 STARS and more!<br /><br />So this what a book hangover feels like?! I have finished this book days ago and I still can’t let go of it. I had to google how to get rid of a book hangover but nothing worked, I mourned with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9536782-ash" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashlee</a> who seems to be just as lost as me, tried other books to abandon after a few chapters.<br /><br />One word for this book, GEM.<br /><br />This novel is uplifting, heart-wrenching and heart-mending. The writing is faultless, the imagery incredible and the connection between our lovers scorching.<br /><br />As I read, it was easy to imagine being part of the epic story that our author created, to experience our protagonists’ every emotion.<br /><br />Our hero was perfect in every way, well to me he was. I know readers relate to books differently and what works for me may not touch other readers as deeply, but Julian was perfection!<br /><br />Julian’s passion, sense of honor, cynicism at times and love are portrayed wonderfully. Ok I’ m going to fangirl a bit more and declare that he is one of ‘BEST HEROES’ I have read about.<br /><br />Our heroine is as interesting and likeable, Emma’s character was a joy to read as well as her journey throughout the book. As a reader, I wanted to ease her pain which I felt alongside with her.<br /><br />They had so many obstacles to overcome, so many things working against that made my heart hurt; I understood what motivated them even though I didn’t agree with a few of their actions.<br /><br />Now let’s talk about the sex scenes, lately I skim those thinking ‘same old same old’ but not with Julian and Emma; reading them gave more glimpses into their characters, besides the fact that I thought they were HOT.<br /><br />I would have loved an epilogue, but that’s because I’m greedy and didn’t want to let Julian and Emma go.<br /><br />I am intrigued by Lockwood’s character and his wife, I googled to see if there is a book written about him yet but found nothing- I would really love to read more about him. I will be trying other books by Ms Duran DEFINITELY.<br /><br />I usually add quotes, but there are so many that I highlighted and you NEED to read this book to experience ever word.<br /><br />Thanks Ash and Suz for the BR. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14527764176383701515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_109352501" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109352501" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2367556-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451733481p2/2367556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109352501?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/2367556-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109352501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10465856568524642998">I love it when I discover a new author and a book that grabs me and keeps me thinking about it long after it is finished. I want a story you can sink your teeth into and one that makes you feel that ache in your chest. This book was just that. Each time I could get a moment to read, I couldn't put it down and only did so because I had to. I am so glad I gave this book a try and would suggest others do the same. I look forward to many more by this author and hope they are every bit as good</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18967379-bookphenomena-micky?shelf=library">library</a>,
